## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics
**Analysis**: This is a chemical kinetics problem seeking the rate law dA/dt as a function of concentration A and time t. The rate law typically involves powers of concentration, but the presence of t suggests possible time-dependent effects, complex mechanisms, or multi-step reactions where intermediates are expressed in terms of t.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 (constant rate, independent of concentration)
- First-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A (rate proportional to concentration)
- Second-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (rate proportional to concentration squared)
- nth-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (general power-law rate dependence)
- Reversible first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 (forward and reverse first-order reactions)
- Reversible second-order to first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 + c1 * A (mixed order terms)
- Autocatalytic rate: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (autocatalytic or logistic-type kinetics)
- Time-dependent first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * t) (rate with time-varying rate constant)
- Parallel reactions: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**2 (competing first and second order pathways)
- Fractional order with offset: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 + c2 (fractional order with constant source/sink)
- Consecutive reaction intermediate: dA_dt = c0 * exp(c1 * t) + c2 * A (production from precursor and self-decay)
- Polynomial rate law: dA_dt = c0 + c1 * A + c2 * A**2 + c3 * A**3 (general polynomial in concentration)
- Inhibition kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A**2) (substrate inhibition model)
- Time-modulated decay: dA_dt = c0 * A * t**c1 (power-law time modulation of rate)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Simple power-law dependence on concentration → nth-order rate law dA_dt = c * A**n, where n is the reaction order
- Linear combination of concentration powers → parallel or competing reaction pathways with different orders
- Product of A and (c - A) terms → autocatalytic or equilibrium-approaching behavior with a carrying capacity
- Exponential time dependence multiplied by concentration → time-varying rate constant, possibly from temperature ramp or photochemical modulation
- Rational functions of A (e.g., A/(1+A^2)) → enzyme-like inhibition or surface saturation with substrate inhibition
- Negative rate values (dA_dt < 0) with magnitude increasing with A → consumption reaction where higher concentration drives faster depletion
- Constant term plus concentration-dependent term → combination of zeroth-order production and higher-order consumption
- Rate depending on both A and t explicitly → non-autonomous kinetics, possibly involving eliminated intermediate species whose concentration varies with time
